**Two new working disciplines added chat 23 (Ray-driven, in response to 4th interrupted-artifact case):**

1. **save-first-not-last** — doc updates happen at milestone boundaries, not chat end. Stub `todo.md` + `status.md` writes at chat start; incremental updates after each milestone. Reverses the chat-19/21/22 failure pattern (saves were ordered *near* the interruption window; this moves them *away* from it).
2. **`support/session.md`** — single-paragraph resume pointer, **first file to read on chat start** before this `todo.md`. Overwritten at every milestone; does not accumulate history (`status.md`'s job). Schema in the file itself.

**Four new conventions added chat 27 (Ray-driven, in response to interruption-rate analysis), effective chat 28+:**

1. **Default to region-scoped reads.** Use `head` / `tail` / `view_range` for lesson HTML, precedent lesson HTML, and precedent SVG — not full-file reads. Build chats were consuming 30–50% more input tokens than necessary. Full-file reads are a deliberate escalation, not the default.
2. **Keep `status.md` chat-N sections concise (~1.5 KB target, not 7 KB).** Disk artifacts are the source of truth; the narrative is annotation. Trim ruthlessly: SVG details visible from the SVG header comment don't need to be repeated; healthy getBBox margins are just "clean."
3. **Intermediate catalog status `built_unwired_chat_N`** between SVG-on-disk and wire-complete. Immediately after the SVG file is written, flip the lesson's catalog entry to `built_unwired_chat_N`. The dominant failure mode (5/5 interrupted-artifact cases) hits exactly the SVG→wire window; this records the build automatically. Effective chat 29+ (next build chat).
4. **Slim chat-N+1 kickoff prompt to ~500 bytes** for build chats; modestly longer for render-check chats (visual-gate content list needs explicit listing). Kickoff structure: project root + UNC reminder + 1 sentence pointing to `session.md` + 1 sentence describing the chat-N task. Working files carry the convention details.

Full rationale and pattern recognition in `status.md` → *Phase 7 progress (chat 27)* → "Conventions added this chat" paragraph + the durable bullets in the *Conventions / things to remember* section.

**One new working discipline added chat 64 startup (Ray-driven, in response to `todo.md` hitting 478 KB after the chat-30 + chat-46 streaming-narrative-in-todo.md discipline's preserved IN-PROGRESS sections accumulated across 18 chats):**

1. **No monolithic accumulator files.** `todo.md` / `status.md` / similar must stay bounded. **Per-chat archive files** are the going-forward pattern: at every chat-N M2 close, the streaming-narrative content of the chat-N IN PROGRESS section gets written to a fresh `support/archive/chat-NN.md` file (one fresh `Filesystem:write_file` call, never re-edited), THEN the IN PROGRESS section in `todo.md` collapses to a 1-paragraph stub (~1.5–2 KB) pointing to the archive file. `todo.md` steady-state target ~80–100 KB. **General principle** (Ray's chat-64-startup direction): "fresh small file > append to existing large file if that will be faster" applies broadly across all working files, not just chat archives. **status.md is FROZEN at chat-60-close** (no further writes; per-chat archive files in `support/archive/` are the going-forward archival pattern from chat 64 onward).

**Chat-64-startup historical cleanup (deferred):** chats 46–63 IN-PROGRESS-style sections in this `todo.md` (~395 KB total) remain in their fat form pending a follow-up cleanup pass; the new discipline takes effect at chat-64 M2 onward (chat 64 will be the first to land its archive in `support/archive/chat-64.md`). Once 5–6 chats have landed under the new discipline, the historical fat sections can be collapsed to stub form in a dedicated cleanup chat.

Three orthogonal axes finalized after lesson body read with **partial confirmation of brief pre-read hypotheses** (TARGETING-EFFECT-TIMING three-mode shape confirmed REPRISE of chat-83 axis 1 with Python-idiomatic dispatch delta; @dataclass TowerStats + Enum TowerType confirmed as Axis 2 candidate at TYPE-CATALOG scope; the brief's WAVES-composition-record-list hypothesis is DECLINED since the lesson's Wave.generate_wave is imperative wave_number-keyed branching not declarative WAVES list — the data-driven externalization at WAVE-COMPOSITION scope from chat-83 doesn't carry forward as Python-idiomatic Wave is imperative; PATH-waypoint-list axis confirmed as Axis 3 candidate at PATH-WAYPOINT scope with Python-idiomatic list-of-tuple delta vs chat-83's JS list-of-object-literal-records): (1) **Snapshot-vs-Live-vs-AOE targeting** at TARGETING-EFFECT-TIMING scope — REPRISE of chat-83 axis 1 with PYTHON-IDIOMATIC consumer-check-distributed dispatch delta. The pygame lesson exposes the same THREE distinct fire-and-effect timing models per tower-type as chat-83 but routes the dispatch differently: PROJECTILE (basic/slow towers) snapshots target position via leading-shot prediction at fire moment using `target.path[target.path_index+1]` next-waypoint sampling + `target.speed * time_to_impact` extrapolation in Projectile.__init__, then projectile flies straight-line toward predicted future point hitting whatever is at that position when it arrives; LASER (laser tower) bypasses Projectile entirely and applies `tower.target.take_damage(tower.stats.damage * tower.level)` directly to the current live target each frame the target is in range — no flight time, no prediction, hits live position; AOE (cannon with splash_radius>0) snapshots target at fire moment but on impact damages all live enemies within splash radius via `enemies` walk with `(1 - distance/splash_radius)` falloff. Python-idiomatic dispatch delta: the type-discrimination happens via `if tower.type == TowerType.LASER:` consumer-check branch IN Game.update's tower-loop rather than via `stats.instant: true` flag check INSIDE Tower.fire as in chat-83's JS — same shape as the chat-82 consumer-check-distributed Python-idiomatic delta from chat-81's centralized JS gating. **CHAT-84 = SECOND-AT-TARGETING-EFFECT-TIMING-SCOPE** (after chat-83's first), expressed in Python-idiomatic style. (2) **Enum-keyed @dataclass-instances-dict at TYPE-CATALOG scope as DOUBLE design-time validation** (Enum membership + @dataclass fields). The pygame lesson's TOWER_STATS = {TowerType.BASIC: TowerStats("Basic Tower", 100, 20, 120, 1.5, 300, BROWN), ...} pairs TWO Python-specific design-time gates that JS plain-string-keyed object literals don't provide: (a) Enum.X membership validated at attribute-access — `TowerType.LSAER` raises AttributeError at parse time vs JS `'lsaer'` silently returning undefined at runtime; (b) @dataclass field declaration validated at construction — missing required arg raises TypeError at instance creation, type hints (`name: str`, `cost: int`, `range: int`, `fire_rate: float`, `projectile_speed: int`, `color: Tuple[int, int, int]`, `splash_radius: int = 0`, etc.) provide static-analyzer hints for typoed field reads. Same DOUBLE-VALIDATION shape as chat-79 dataclass-roundtrip wrinkle (skill prerequisites Enum + dataclass round-tripped through JSON serialization) and chat-82 Enum-keyed stats dict (UnitStats Enum-keyed dict with frozen contract), here at TYPE-CATALOG scope where the design-time hypothesis is 'this tower/enemy type exists with these stats' and the runtime discovery is 'AttributeError on a typoed Enum member or TypeError on a missing required dataclass field at construction time'. **CHAT-84 = EIGHTH design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery lesson** after chat-47 platformer_level_design (validate vs is_solid) + chat-70 publishing_executables (hidden_imports static-AST-vs-runtime) + chat-72 publishing_performance (profile-bars vs intuition) + chat-73 publishing_platforms (capability detection) + chat-76 genres_puzzle_python (Enum-vs-isinstance dispatch) + chat-79 genres_rpg_python (Enum-roundtrip-vs-live-comparison) + chat-82 genres_strategy_python (Enum-keyed UNIT_STATS) = 7 prior cases; chat-84 is the EIGHTH and FIRST applied at TYPE-CATALOG scope where Enum + @dataclass STACK to provide TWO orthogonal validation gates rather than one. (3) **PATH-waypoint-list at PATH-WAYPOINT scope (Python list-of-tuple idiom)** — REPRISE of chat-83 axis 2 with Python-idiomatic list-of-tuple delta vs chat-83's JS list-of-object-literal-records. The 8-record `PATH: List[Tuple[int, int]] = [(0, 400), (200, 400), (200, 200), (500, 200), (500, 500), (700, 500), (700, 300), (SCREEN_WIDTH, 300)]` IS the canonical route definition that ALL consumers iterate over by index: `Enemy.update` consumes by `self.path_index` walking path[path_index+1] for next-waypoint movement, `Projectile.__init__` consumes by `target.path[target.path_index+1]` for leading-shot prediction, `Game.draw` walks `self.path[i]` to `self.path[i+1]` for path rendering, `Game.can_place_tower` walks pairs as bounding-box rectangles for path-collision prevention. Adding/changing the route is one list edit and ALL consumers pick it up automatically because they iterate or index into the same list rather than branching on hardcoded coordinates. Same data-driven-externalization shape as chat-83 axis 2 (PATH-WAYPOINT-LIST scope) here in Python-idiomatic list-of-tuple form. **M1 plan:** distill all three pillars into one runnable pygame program (~85–95 lines, pygame-companion size matching chat-76/79/82). Three orthogonal axes finalized after lesson body read, with **partial confirmation of brief pre-read hypotheses** (PATH-waypoint axis confirmed; WAVES-composition axis confirmed; the brief's targeting-effect-timing extension is confirmed but at a richer 3-mode shape than the simple snapshot-vs-homing pre-read; the brief's tower-upgrade-tier candidate axis declined since the lesson's `Tower.upgrade()` is just `level`-multiplier with consumer-check `damage * level` at call sites, not strong enough as a third orthogonal axis competing with TARGETING-EFFECT-TIMING + PATH-WAYPOINT + WAVES-COMPOSITION): (1) **Snapshot-vs-live-vs-AOE targeting** at TARGETING-EFFECT-TIMING scope — CONTEXT-DETERMINES-CORRECT-CHOICE pattern; the lesson exposes THREE distinct fire-and-effect timing models per tower-type: PROJECTILE (basic/slow towers) snapshots target position via leading-shot prediction at fire moment then projectile flies toward predicted future point hitting whatever is at that position when it arrives — fire-and-forget commits to predicted future at fire time; INSTANT (laser tower with `stats.instant: true`) bypasses projectile entirely and deals damage directly to current live target via `LaserBeam` particle — no flight time, no prediction, hits live position; AOE (cannon with `stats.splash`) snapshots target at fire moment but on impact damages all live enemies within splash radius — combines snapshot-at-fire with live-spatial-query-at-impact. **CHAT-83 = SECOND-AT-EFFECT-TIMING-FAMILY-SCOPE** (after chat-81's snapshot-at-research and chat-82's retroactive-at-research at RESEARCH-EFFECT-TIMING scope), FIRST applied at TARGETING-EFFECT-TIMING scope where the timing-model determines per-shot gameplay rhythm rather than per-research-event gameplay rhythm. Different gameplay rhythms produced: predictive projectile encourages strategic placement (towers shoot ahead, well-placed towers compensate for enemy speed); instant laser encourages reactive placement (laser hits whatever's in range NOW, single-target high-DPS); AOE cannon encourages choke-point placement (clustered enemies all take splash). Same context-determines-correct-choice rhetoric as chat-49 polish_tweening / chat-50 polish_difficulty / chat-50 polish_playtesting / chat-52 client_server / chat-53 lag_compensation / chat-54 lobby / chat-60 pathfinding heuristic / chat-61 Selector vs Sequence / chat-62 utility-AI vs BT / chat-63 flocking emergence / chat-79 enum-roundtrip-vs-live-comparison / chat-81 snapshot-at-research / chat-82 retroactive-at-research, applied here at TARGETING-EFFECT-TIMING scope with three-mode shape rather than two-mode binary. (2) **PATH-waypoint-list data-driven externalization** at PATH-WAYPOINT-LIST scope — DATA-DRIVEN EXTERNALIZATION pattern; the module-level `PATH` array (8 `{x, y}` records describing the S-curve) IS the canonical route definition that ALL consumers iterate over: `Enemy.update()` consumes by `pathIndex` for movement, `Projectile` constructor consumes by `target.pathIndex + 1` for leading-shot prediction, `isValidTowerPosition()` consumes by walking pairs `(p1, p2)` to test 'tower not on path', and the rendering loop draws path segments by walking `PATH[i]` to `PATH[i+1]`. Adding/changing the route is one array edit and ALL consumers pick it up automatically because they iterate or index into the same array rather than branching on hardcoded coordinates. Same data-driven-externalization shape as the long second-half-Phase-8 streak (chat-46 platformer_tilemap is_solid + chat-47 tile-palette + chat-54 explicit transition table + chat-55 scene-stack lifecycle hooks + chat-56 required-components list + chat-57 listeners-by-event dict + chat-58 dataclass schema + chat-59 per-state perception + chat-60 TERRAIN_COST dict + chat-61 RUNNING-state stickiness + Selector child-list order + chat-62 personality dict + chat-63 local-rule additive forces + chat-79 skill-prerequisites + chat-81 UNIT_STATS object literal + chat-82 Enum-keyed stats dict), **chat-83 = SEVENTEENTH-AT-DATA-DRIVEN-EXTERNALIZATION-FAMILY** applied at PATH-WAYPOINT-LIST scope where the route IS data the rendering, movement, prediction, and placement-validation systems all consume in lockstep. Matches brief pre-read hypothesis ('waypoint-based path-following potentially extending chat-46 platformer_tilemap data-driven externalization at PATH-WAYPOINT-LIST scope'). (3) **WAVES-composition-record-list data-driven externalization with declarative per-group spacing** at WAVE-COMPOSITION-DICT scope — DATA-DRIVEN EXTERNALIZATION pattern; the module-level `WAVES` array (10 records, each `{enemies: [{type, count, spacing}, ...]}`) IS the canonical wave-pacing declaration that `class WaveSpawner` consumes by flattening wave-record into per-enemy `enemyQueues` list then time-walking via `now - this.lastSpawn > enemyData.delay` to spawn enemies at declared per-group cadence. Adding a new wave is ONE record edit (e.g. `{enemies: [{type: 'tank', count: 3, spacing: 1500}, {type: 'flying', count: 5, spacing: 800}]}`); the spawner picks it up automatically because it iterates the array by `WAVES[Math.min(waveNumber, WAVES.length - 1)]`. **chat-83 = EIGHTEENTH-AT-DATA-DRIVEN-EXTERNALIZATION-FAMILY** applied at WAVES-COMPOSITION-DICT scope where each wave is a declarative record describing what spawns and how fast — same data-driven-externalization shape as chat-58 schema-as-frozen-contract upgraded to wave-as-frozen-record with mixed-enemy-group composition, AND extends Axis 2's per-route data-driven-externalization at PATH-WAYPOINT scope by composing into MULTI-WAVE timeline data. Matches brief pre-read hypothesis ('wave-spawning timing logic potentially extending chat-60 ai_pathfinding TERRAIN_COST dict externalization at WAVE-COMPOSITION-DICT scope'). **M1 plan: distill all three pillars into one runnable canvas + JS program (~65–75 lines, JS-canvas size matching chat-75/77/78/81 not pygame size).** Title: 'Three Pillars of Tower Defense Architecture — Snapshot-vs-Live-vs-AOE Targeting + PATH-Waypoint-List + WAVES-Composition-Record-List in One Canvas Window'. Single 900×420 canvas with three integrated regions sharing one scene: small `PATH = [...5 waypoints...]` data with R-key swap to alternate route from a 2-entry ROUTES dict (Axis 2 visible — PATH array drives routing for ALL consumers); 3 towers placed beside the path each demonstrating one timing-model — projectile-tower (snapshot+lead) firing yellow projectiles that fly to predicted future positions, laser-tower (live) firing instant cyan beams to current target positions, cannon-tower (AOE) firing red projectiles to predicted positions then `splash`-damaging all enemies within radius on impact (Axis 1 visible — three timing models side-by-side); compact `WAVES = [...3 short waves...]` data with W key to start next wave from queue, HUD shows currently-spawning enemy types and remaining count per wave (Axis 3 visible — wave-composition data declares pacing for ALL spawn logic). HUD shows tower-mode legend (P/L/A — projectile snapshot, laser live, cannon AOE), current PATH route active (A or B), current wave + enemies remaining, three-axis legend. Full-stem h2 id `practice-exercise-build-genres-tower-defense` per the established convention (already present in the scaffold so just preserve it); literal U+2014 em-dash codepoint (29th consecutive); shape-2 outer-single-quote attribute values (29th consecutive); HTML-escape `&lt;`/`&gt;` inside `<pre><code>` (42nd consecutive). ### Milestone narrative (streaming, chat 82)

**M0 (181st save-first step) — completed end-to-end clean.** Finding-10 EXTRA-SCRUTINY pre-check on `genres_strategy_python.html` per chat-62/63 .bak-baseline date+size refinement: `.html` = 42,726 bytes modified Tue May 05 2026 05:04:40 PDT; `.bak` = 40,103 bytes modified Wed Apr 29 2026 13:45:15 PDT; delta = +2,623 bytes (consistent with chat-39 TBD scaffold range ~2.5–3 KB); `.bak` modified date predates `.html` modified date — **ANCHOR-CLEAN** as anticipated. Note: brief's prior-cohort recollection of absolute byte sizes (~22,787 B for both files) is stale — actual sizes are nearly 2× the brief's estimate because `genres_strategy_python` is a content-richer pygame-implementation lesson than the brief's recollection assumed (full ~610-line pygame implementation including A* pathfinding heapq class, AIController with 4 strategy branches, 6 building types, 5 unit types, fog-of-war reveal, tech-tree dispatch); the relative delta and date ordering — which is what Finding-10 actually tests — are clean. Third pygame-companion lesson (chat-76 + chat-79 + chat-82) reinforcing the genres-pygame-mostly-ANCHOR-CLEAN pattern. Catalog target verification via `Filesystem:edit_file --dryRun=true` no-op self-replace required ONE refinement attempt: initial dryRun against the brief's hypothesized 5-key `quiz_drafted` shape (`status` → `module` → `completed_chat: null` → `exercise_card_objective: null` → `quiz_topics: null`) failed to match; cross-checking the cached catalog dump revealed the actual `quiz_drafted` shape is **4-key** (no `completed_chat` field at all in `quiz_drafted` form — that key only appears in the `done` form where it carries the integer chat number); revised dryRun against the 4-key shape (`status: 'quiz_drafted'`, `module: 'genres'`, `exercise_card_objective: null`, `quiz_topics: null`) returned empty diff confirming entry at exact expected state — **22nd consecutive object-form-shape target verification clean** (with one-time shape-refinement that the brief's verification recipe will be amended for going forward; the chat-82 M1 catalog flip therefore promotes 4-key → 5-key by ADDING the `completed_chat: 82` field at position 3 alongside flipping `status` to `'done'` and filling `exercise_card_objective` and `quiz_topics`). Lesson body region read confirms pygame implementation as hypothesized (NOT JS-canvas; chat-81 cohort-36 = `genres_strategy.html` was the JS-canvas companion); ~610 lines of inline `<pre class="language-python"><code>` covering an 800×600 pygame window with `class UnitType(Enum)` + `class BuildingType(Enum)` for type identity, `@dataclass Resources` value-object with `gold/food/wood: int = 0` fields and `can_afford` / `subtract` / `add` arithmetic methods, `class Unit` whose constructor reads `stats[unit_type]` from a local dict literal keyed by `UnitType` Enum members, `class Building` with parallel BuildingType-keyed stats dict + `construction_progress: int = 100; is_complete: bool = True` defaults flipped to `0; False` at `build_structure()` call site, `class Map` with terrain/fog/`reveal()`, `class Pathfinding` static-method A* with heapq, `class AIController` with rule-based strategy dispatch over balanced/aggressive/defensive/economic, `class StrategyGame` orchestrator with `unit_costs: dict[UnitType, Resources]` + `building_costs: dict[BuildingType, Resources]` + `tech_tree: dict[str, dict]` cost/effect records, `update(dt)` walks units (movement + combat + cooldown + death) then walks buildings (construction ramp + production queue + resource generation + tower attack + death), and `research_tech(name)` applies tech effects RETROACTIVELY by walking all extant units/buildings and mutating their stats in place. Three orthogonal axes finalized after lesson body read, with **partial divergence from brief pre-read hypotheses** (which mentioned `Protocol`/`asdict`-roundtrip / 7th design-time-validation lesson at TYPE-IDENTITY scope / snapshot-vs-retroactive timing — first two don't appear in the lesson code as `typing.Protocol` is not imported and `asdict` is not called anywhere; third does appear but the lesson picks the OPPOSITE side from chat-81): (1) **Building-lifecycle gate at `is_complete` boolean checked at every consumer site** at BUILDING-LIFECYCLE scope — strict-ordering / design-time-vs-runtime / fail-safe-defaults pattern; `Building.update()` ramps `construction_progress += 1` per frame until `>= 100` then flips `is_complete = True` AND calls `map.reveal()` exclusively at the moment of completion; downstream consumers (`production_queue` step, `generates` step, `BuildingType.TOWER` attack step) ALL guard via `if building.is_complete:` checks. **Python-idiomatic delta from chat-81's `onComplete()` method**: chat-81 (JS) centralized the side-effects into one `onComplete()` method called exactly once at the moment progress crossed 100; chat-82 (Python) distributes the side-effect-gating across N consumer-site checks. Both are valid; the JS-vs-Python implementations differ at the call-site-distribution-vs-callback-centralization level even though the architectural intent is identical (gate side effects on lifecycle completion). Same default-to-deny-at-the-boundary shape as chat-46 platformer_tilemap's is_solid-True-OOB invariant + chat-54 architecture_state_machines' on_exit→reassign→on_enter strict ordering + chat-56 architecture_component_systems' components-hold-state-systems-hold-per-tick-logic separation + chat-57 architecture_event_systems' queued-emit-vs-immediate-emit timing modes + chat-81 genres_strategy onComplete-as-gate, applied here at BUILDING-LIFECYCLE scope with the consumer-check Python-idiomatic delta. (2) **`Enum`-keyed stats dict at UNIT-AND-BUILDING-TYPE-DEFINITION scope** — DATA-DRIVEN EXTERNALIZATION + DESIGN-TIME-VALIDATION-VS-RUNTIME-DISCOVERY pattern; both `Unit` and `Building` constructors hold a per-type dict literal keyed by `UnitType` / `BuildingType` Enum MEMBERS (not string literals): `stats = { UnitType.WORKER: {hp:50, attack:5, ...}, UnitType.SOLDIER: {hp:100, attack:15, ...}, ... }` then `unit_stats = stats[unit_type]; self.hp = unit_stats['hp']` etc. **Python-idiomatic delta from chat-81's `UNIT_STATS = { worker: {...}, ... }` JS object-literal**: chat-82 uses Enum members as keys, which means a typo at the spawn site (`Unit(UnitType.WROKER, ...)`) raises `AttributeError: type object 'UnitType' has no attribute 'WROKER'` at IMPORT/PARSE time before the constructor even runs; the equivalent JS typo (`new Unit('wroker', ...)`) silently produces a unit with all-undefined stats that crashes much later at first attribute access or, worse, runs as a glitched zero-stat unit. The Enum-member-as-key shape upgrades chat-81's data-driven-externalization pattern with design-time-validation at the key-lookup site — same SEVENTH design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery lesson axis as chat-47 platformer_level_design + chat-70 publishing_executables + chat-72 publishing_performance + chat-73 publishing_platforms + chat-76 genres_puzzle_python + chat-79 genres_rpg_python = 6 prior cases, chat-82 = 7th, FIRST applied at STATS-DICT-KEY-IDENTITY scope where Enum-member-as-key replaces string-as-key. Same data-driven-externalization shape as the long second-half-Phase-8 streak (chat-46 is_solid + chat-47 tile-palette + chat-54 explicit transition table + chat-55 scene-stack lifecycle hooks + chat-56 required-components list + chat-57 listeners-by-event dict + chat-58 dataclass schema + chat-59 per-state perception + chat-60 TERRAIN_COST dict + chat-61 RUNNING-state stickiness + Selector child-list order + chat-62 personality dict + chat-63 local-rule additive forces + chat-79 skill-prerequisites declarative records + chat-81 RTS UNIT_STATS object-literal). (3) **Retroactive research bonus applied to all extant units once at research moment, NOT snapshotted at creation time** at RESEARCH-EFFECT-TIMING scope — CONTEXT-DETERMINES-CORRECT-CHOICE pattern; `research_tech('military_training')` walks `for unit in self.units: unit.attack = int(unit.attack * 1.2)` mutating every extant unit's attack stat IN PLACE at the moment research completes, with NO corresponding hook in `Unit.__init__` to consult `self.researched_techs` for future spawns. **OPPOSITE design choice from chat-81**: chat-81's RTS research used SNAPSHOT-AT-CREATION-TIME (each `Unit` constructor checked `if (gameState.researched.has('military')) { this.attack *= 1.25 }` at construction, so future spawns get the bonus and extant units retain baseline); chat-82's RTS research uses LIVE-RETROACTIVE (`research_tech` mutates extant units, future spawns get baseline). Both are legitimate design choices producing different gameplay rhythms — snapshot encourages 'tech-up THEN rebuild' army-replacement pacing (AoE2-style late-game cycle); retroactive encourages 'tech-up empowers your existing army immediately' instant-effect pacing (Civ-style instant-tech). The chat-82 lesson picking the OPPOSITE side from chat-81 is a deliberate pedagogical contrast that lets the JS-then-pygame paired companion lessons demonstrate the SAME architectural axis (RESEARCH-EFFECT-TIMING) from BOTH sides of the design-spectrum, making the context-determines-correct-choice rhetoric visible as the pair. Same context-determines-correct-choice rhetoric as the long second-half-Phase-8 run (chat-49 polish_tweening + chat-50 polish_difficulty/playtesting + chat-52 client_server + chat-53 lag_compensation + chat-54 lobby + chat-60 pathfinding heuristic + chat-61 Selector vs Sequence + chat-62 utility-AI vs BT + chat-63 flocking emergence + chat-79 enum-roundtrip-vs-live-comparison + chat-81 snapshot-vs-retroactive at RESEARCH-EFFECT-TIMING scope), chat-82 = SECOND-AT-RESEARCH-EFFECT-TIMING-SCOPE (after chat-81) and FIRST to demonstrate the contrasting RETROACTIVE side at this scope. **M1 plan: distill all three pillars into one runnable pygame program (~80–90 lines, pygame-companion size matching chat-76/79).** Title: 'Three Pillars of Python RTS Architecture — Construction-Gate-at-is_complete + Enum-Keyed-Stats-Dict + Retroactive-Research-Bonus in One Pygame Window'. Single 1088×540 window with three vertical panels (each ~362 wide, thin separators): LEFT panel renders 3 buildings under construction (Mine / Farm / Barracks) with progress bars + 'global income' tally that stays at 0 until each building's `is_complete` flips True then ticks at that building's per-second rate (Axis A visible — `if b.is_complete: gold += b.income_per_sec * dt` consumer-check pattern); MIDDLE panel renders unit-spawn area where keys 1/2/3 spawn worker/soldier/archer using module-level `UNIT_STATS: dict[UnitType, dict]` Enum-keyed lookup, with H key mutating `UNIT_STATS[UnitType.SOLDIER]['hp'] += 20` at runtime so the next-spawned soldier shows the new HP while extant soldiers retain old HP (Axis B visible — Enum-key design-time-validation at IDENTITY scope, runtime-mutation propagating only to subsequent constructions); RIGHT panel renders pre-spawned cohort of 3 soldiers each at baseline attack=15, with R key triggering retroactive research_tech walk that mutates all 3 in place to attack=18 (15*1.2 rounded down by `int()`) — visible as HUD readout 'Pre-R: [15,15,15] | Post-R: [18,18,18]' (Axis C visible — retroactive at moment-of-research, not snapshot at moment-of-spawn). HUD shows time, gold income tally, current `UNIT_STATS[UnitType.SOLDIER]['hp']` value, research-on/off flag, and the legend. Catalog target verified clean via `Filesystem:edit_file --dryRun=true` no-op self-replace on the expected `quiz_drafted` shape (`status: 'quiz_drafted'`, `module: 'genres'`, `exercise_card_objective: null`, `quiz_topics: null`) — empty diff confirms entry at exact expected state, 22nd consecutive object-form-shape target verification. Lesson body region read confirms HTML5-canvas + JS implementation as hypothesized (NOT pygame; pygame companion is chat-81 cohort-37 = `genres_strategy_python.html`); ~600 lines of inline `<script>` covering an 800×600 canvas with 50×50 tile map, `GameMap` class (terrain variety + per-tile `fogOfWar` boolean + `revealArea(x,y,radius)` permanent reveal — no re-fog), `Unit` class (worker/soldier/archer/cavalry/siege drawn from a per-type stats dict literal then `Object.assign(this, unitStats)`), `Building` class (base/barracks/mine/farm/tower/wall drawn from a parallel per-type stats dict with `income`/`provides`/`canProduce`/`attack`/`defense`/`range` optional fields), `Effect` class (projectile particles), `AIController` class (rule-based opponent with `actionTimer` triggering `makeDecision` every 3 seconds), `gameState` tracking resources/income/researched-Set/population, build/train/research onclick handler chain, camera with WASD/arrow-key pan + mouse-wheel zoom, `gameLoop` with `deltaTime`-driven update + render. Three orthogonal axes finalized after lesson body read, with **significant divergence from brief pre-read hypotheses** (which mentioned tech-tree-as-prerequisite-DAG / AI-decision-priority-as-weighted-list / resource-flow-as-rate-limited-counters — none of those are the dominant axes in the actual code; the brief flagged 'CHECK LESSON CONTENT FIRST' precisely because the strategy-genre topic admits many architectural decompositions and the lesson's chosen pillars only emerge from the body): (1) **Building-lifecycle gate at `onComplete()`** at BUILDING-LIFECYCLE scope — strict-ordering / design-time-vs-runtime / fail-safe-defaults pattern; `Building.update()` ramps `constructionProgress += deltaTime * 2` until ≥ 100 then flips `isComplete = true` AND calls `this.onComplete()` which is the exclusive site that writes `gameState.income[resource] += amount`, increments `gameState.maxPopulation`, and calls `gameMap.revealArea(this.x + this.size/2, this.y + this.size/2, this.sight)`. During construction (progress < 100) the building exists on the map and occupies its tile but contributes ZERO income to the global tally, ZERO maxPopulation contribution, and ZERO sight reveal — the income/maxPopulation/sight effects strictly FOLLOW completion. The two-layer separation (data: income amount in stats dict; gate: `isComplete` boolean check) is exactly the same shape as chat-46 platformer_tilemap's is_solid-True-OOB invariant (default-to-deny at the boundary), chat-54 architecture_state_machines' on_exit→reassign→on_enter strict ordering, chat-56 architecture_component_systems' components-hold-state-systems-hold-per-tick-logic separation, chat-57 architecture_event_systems' queued-emit-vs-immediate-emit timing modes, applied here at building-construction-lifecycle scope. (2) **Stats-table externalization at UNIT/BUILDING-TYPE-DEFINITION scope** — DATA-DRIVEN EXTERNALIZATION; both `Unit` and `Building` constructors hold a per-type dict literal: `const stats = { worker: {hp:50, attack:5, speed:1.5, range:1, sight:5}, soldier: {hp:100, attack:15, ...}, archer: {hp:60, attack:12, range:5, sight:8}, cavalry: {hp:120, speed:2}, siege: {hp:200, attack:50, range:6} }; Object.assign(this, stats[type] || stats.soldier);` and a parallel building stats dict with optional `income`/`provides`/`canProduce`/`attack`/`defense`/`range` fields keyed by type. Adding a new unit type ('mage', 'healer', 'spy') is ONE dict entry rather than scattered if/elif edits across `update()` / `render()` / `findPath()` / collision / production. Same data-driven-externalization shape as the long second-half-Phase-8 streak — chat-46 is_solid + chat-47 tile-palette JSON + chat-54 explicit transition table + chat-55 scene-stack lifecycle hooks + chat-56 required-components list + chat-57 listeners-by-event dict + chat-58 dataclass schema + chat-59 per-state perception + chat-60 TERRAIN_COST dict + chat-61 RUNNING-state stickiness + Selector child-list order + chat-62 personality-as-weighted-modifier dict + chat-63 local-rule additive forces + chat-79 skill-prerequisites-as-declarative-data-records — applied here at UNIT-AND-BUILDING-TYPE-DEFINITION scope (the stats dict IS the canonical per-type definition the constructor consults exactly once per spawn). (3) **Research bonus applied at creation time, not retroactively** at RESEARCH-EFFECT-TIMING scope — CONTEXT-DETERMINES-CORRECT-CHOICE pattern; the `Unit` constructor checks `if (gameState.researched.has('military')) { this.attack *= 1.25; this.maxHp *= 1.1; this.hp = this.maxHp; }` AT CONSTRUCTION TIME so a unit spawned BEFORE military research keeps its baseline stats forever; only units spawned AFTER receive the bonus. The `Building` constructor does the parallel thing with `if (gameState.researched.has('defense')) { this.maxHp *= 1.25; if (this.defense) this.defense *= 1.5; }` and `if (gameState.researched.has('economy') && this.income) { *= 1.25 }`. The alternative architecture — live retroactive multiplier walking every extant unit/building after research completes — is a legitimately different design choice with different gameplay rhythm: snapshot timing produces 'tech-up-THEN-rebuild' pacing where players must replace existing units to fully benefit (think AoE2's late-game army-replacement cycle); live timing produces 'research instantly empowers everything' pacing (think Civ's instant-tech-effect model). Both are valid; the lesson picks snapshot as a deliberate architectural choice. Same context-determines-correct-choice rhetoric as chat-49 polish_tweening / chat-50 polish_difficulty / chat-50 polish_playtesting / chat-52 client_server / chat-53 lag_compensation / chat-54 lobby / chat-60 pathfinding heuristic / chat-61 Selector vs Sequence / chat-62 utility-AI vs BT / chat-63 flocking emergence / chat-79 enum-roundtrip-vs-live-comparison-by-name — chat-80 case is FIRST to make the snapshot-vs-retroactive distinction explicit at RESEARCH-EFFECT-TIMING scope. **M1 plan: distill all three pillars into one runnable canvas + JS program (~60–65 lines, JS-canvas size matching chat-75/77/78 not pygame size).** Title: 'Three Pillars of RTS Architecture — Construction-Gate-at-onComplete + Stats-Table-Externalization + Snapshot-Research-Bonus in One Canvas Window'. Single 800×420 canvas with three labeled regions: LEFT renders 3 buildings under construction with per-building progress bars + 'global income' readout that stays at 0 until each building's progress hits 100 then ticks up at that building's per-second rate (Axis A visible — onComplete is the gate that flips); MIDDLE renders unit-spawn area where keys 1/2/3 spawn worker/soldier/archer using `UNIT_STATS[type]` dict literal lookup, with a '+HP' key (H) that mutates `UNIT_STATS.soldier.hp += 20` at runtime so the next-spawned soldier shows the new HP while extant soldiers retain old HP (Axis B visible — stats-table externalization, mutation propagates ONLY to subsequent spawns); RIGHT renders a research panel with R key that flips `gameState.researched.add('military')` AND each unit's constructor snapshots whether the bonus was active at its spawn moment, so old units pre-R retain baseline attack while new units post-R show `attack *= 1.25` boost (Axis C visible — snapshot at creation time, never retroactively). HUD shows time, total income, soldier-count pre-R vs post-R with avg attack per cohort, current `UNIT_STATS.soldier.hp` value. Full-stem h2 id `practice-exercise-build-genres-strategy` per the established convention; literal U+2014 em-dash codepoint (27th consecutive); shape-2 outer-single-quote attribute values (27th consecutive); HTML-escape `&lt;`/`&gt;` inside `<pre><code>` (40th consecutive). Quality-flag carry-forward (architecture_save_load.html UTF-8 corruption) deferred again per established pattern (22nd consecutive deferral). Proceeding to M1.

The next-lesson nav points to `genres_strategy.html` (correctly previewing chat-80's recommended cohort). **Three Python-specific deltas confirmed after lesson body read, with significant divergence from the chat-79 brief's pre-read hypotheses:** (1) the lesson uses `@dataclass`-decorated Character/Item/Quest classes with `asdict(self.character)` in save_game() walking the dataclass fields recursively producing a JSON-serializable dict matching the field names exactly (chat-78's JS lesson did `JSON.stringify({character, inventory, quests})` against unstructured object literals, NO field-list discipline); (2) the lesson uses `class CharacterClass(Enum)` and `class ItemType(Enum)` with both `ItemType.CONSUMABLE`/`ItemType.WEAPON` static-name references AND `CharacterClass(char_data['char_class'])` / `ItemType(item_data['item_type'])` Enum-from-string-value reconstructors at load time — raising ValueError if the saved string doesn't match a declared Enum member; (3) the lesson does NOT use `typing.Protocol` or ABC for an equipment-slot interface (no shared protocol declared anywhere; equipment is a plain dict `inventory.equipment[slot]`), does NOT use `collections.deque` for combat queue (combat is single-attacker-single-target via perform_attack with no queue), does NOT use `itertools` for grid traversal (no grid in this file at all), and does NOT use polymorphic dispatch for skill behavior (skills are inert data records with a Skill.learn() method that applies stat increments via `setattr(character, stat, current + value)` reflection-style writes). **Brief's pre-read hypotheses (a) dataclass-Character matches partially (dataclass IS used, but the design lever is the asdict-roundtrip not just the @dataclass decoration), (b) Protocol-equipment-slot DID NOT match (no Protocol used), (c) Enum-character-class matches AND extends to ItemType (two Enum applications, both with string-roundtrip), and the predicted dict-based skill-tree-with-string-encoded-prerequisites MATCHES (Skill.requirements is a List[Dict] with skill_id+level keys); revised three orthogonal axes after lesson body read:** (a) **Enum-roundtrip-through-save at CHARACTER-CLASS-AND-ITEM-TYPE IDENTITY scope** — `class CharacterClass(Enum)` and `class ItemType(Enum)` enumerate valid identities at design-time so a typo `ItemType.CONSUM` raises AttributeError at the import statement of the typo-containing module; the Enum-from-string-value reconstructors `CharacterClass(char_data['char_class'])` and `ItemType(item_data['item_type'])` round-trip the saved JSON string back to a strongly-typed Enum member at load time, raising ValueError if the saved string doesn't match a declared member — making save-file format drift a LOAD-TIME exception rather than a silent runtime corruption (e.g., if `CharacterClass.WIZARD` is renamed to `CharacterClass.MAGE` between game versions, an old save with 'wizard' string blows up at load instead of silently constructing a Character with no behavior); same design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery pattern as chat-47 platformer_level_design's validate-vs-is_solid + chat-70 publishing_executables's hiddenimports static-AST-vs-runtime-discovery + chat-72 publishing_performance's profile-bars-vs-intuition + chat-73 publishing_platforms's try-import runtime-capability-detection + chat-76 genres_puzzle_python's PuzzleType-Enum applied at CHARACTER-CLASS-AND-ITEM-TYPE IDENTITY scope = **SIXTH lesson reinforcing the design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery pattern across Phase 8, FIRST applied at IDENTITY scope with ROUND-TRIP-THROUGH-SAVE wrinkle that chat-76's PuzzleType Enum did not exercise** since chat-76's enum was used only for in-memory dispatch with no save/load round-trip. **(This axis is a refinement of the chat-79 brief's pre-read hypothesis (c) Enum-character-class with the round-trip-through-save extension as the architecturally distinguishing lever beyond mere identity enumeration.)** (b) **Dataclass-asdict serialization as schema-IS-the-class at SAVE-FORMAT scope** — `'character': asdict(self.character)` works because Character is `@dataclass`-decorated; asdict() walks the dataclass fields recursively producing a JSON-serializable dict whose keys EXACTLY match the dataclass field names; `'slots': [asdict(item) if item else None for item in self.inventory.slots]` does the same for each Item dataclass per inventory slot; the save format IS the dataclass field set with no parallel "save schema" definition to keep in sync — adding a new field to Character automatically adds it to save files, removing a field automatically removes it, renaming a field breaks load-time dict access at exactly the field that drifted; the on-the-load reverse `Character(char_data['name'], CharacterClass(char_data['char_class']))` reconstructs through the constructor + Enum-roundtrip and then `for key, value in char_data.items(): if hasattr(self.character, key): setattr(self.character, key, value)` propagates the remaining fields via reflection-style writes; same schema-as-frozen-contract pattern as chat-58 architecture_save_load applied at SAVE-FORMAT scope where the dataclass field declarations ARE the save schema rather than living as a parallel JSON schema document. **(This axis takes the chat-79 brief's pre-read hypothesis (a) slot but reframes — the lesson's actual lever is the asdict-roundtrip making the dataclass field declaration the single source of truth for the save format, not just the @dataclass decoration as an isolated feature.)** (c) **Skill-prerequisites-as-declarative-data-records at SKILL-TREE-VALIDATION scope** — `self.requirements = [{'skill_id': 'power_strike', 'level': 3}]` is declarative data the `Skill.can_learn()` method iterates through (`for req in self.requirements: req_skill = skill_tree.get_skill(req['skill_id']); if not req_skill or req_skill.level < req['level']: return False`) to check prerequisites; adding a new prerequisite to an existing skill is a single `requirements.append({'skill_id': X, 'level': N})` call; adding a new skill with prerequisites is a single Skill construction + `self.requirements = [...]` assignment with ZERO changes to `can_learn()`'s control flow. The alternative — hardcoding requirements as if-elif chains in `can_learn()` per skill (`if self.id == 'berserker': if not skill_tree.skills.get('power_strike') or skill_tree.skills['power_strike'].level < 3: return False; elif self.id == 'teleport': ...; elif self.id == 'mana_shield': ...`) — would scatter prerequisite logic across the class, force every new skill to add a new elif branch, and prevent multi-prerequisite skills from being expressed cleanly (the data-records form trivially handles `requirements = [{'skill_id': 'A', 'level': 3}, {'skill_id': 'B', 'level': 2}]`); same data-driven externalization pattern as architecture_save_load schema chat-58 + pathfinding terrain-cost dict chat-60 + behavior-trees child-list-order chat-61 + decision-making personality dict chat-62 + procedural generation seed chat-68 + publishing_executables .spec chat-70 + publishing_marketing pitch templates chat-71 + publishing_performance algorithmic-axis chat-72 + publishing_platforms TARGETS+ADAPTERS chat-73 + publishing_updates CADENCES+MIGRATIONS chat-74 + genres_puzzle 2D-array board chat-75 + genres_puzzle_python 2D-array board chat-76 + genres_racing TRACKS dict chat-77 + genres_rpg dialogue-graph chat-78 applied at SKILL-TREE-VALIDATION scope = **TWENTY-FIRST lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8, FIRST applied at SKILL-TREE-VALIDATION scope** where the prerequisite list IS data the validator iterates through. **(This axis was not in the chat-79 brief's pre-read hypotheses but matches what the lesson actually demonstrates as a third orthogonal architectural lever; the brief's pre-read hypothesis (b) Protocol-equipment-slot did NOT match what the lesson shows since no Protocol is declared anywhere in the file.)** Cross-references chat-58 architecture_save_load (schema-as-frozen-contract carry-forward applied to SAVE-FORMAT scope at axis (b) where the dataclass field set IS the save schema), chat-76 genres_puzzle_python (Enum-based identity at PUZZLE-IDENTITY scope adjacent to chat-79's at CHARACTER-CLASS-AND-ITEM-TYPE IDENTITY scope at axis (a), with chat-79 adding the round-trip-through-save extension), and chat-78 genres_rpg (the JS-implementation predecessor; chat-78's NARRATIVE-FLOW dialogue-tree-as-index-pointer-graph at axis (a) extends to chat-79's SKILL-TREE-VALIDATION skill-prerequisites-as-data at axis (c) since both are graph-shaped data structures the renderer/validator iterates through, but at distinct scopes). **Brief's pre-read hypothesis about `collections.deque` for combat queue, `itertools` for grid traversal, dict-based polymorphic skill-tree dispatch, and pygame event-loop-with-polymorphic-dispatch ALL DID NOT match what the lesson actually shows** — combat is single-attacker-single-target with no queue (deque unnecessary), there's no grid in the file (itertools unnecessary), skill-tree is data-records-iterated-through not polymorphic-dispatch-based, and the pygame run() loop dispatches to render_inventory/render_quests via plain if-checks on show_inventory/show_quests booleans rather than polymorphic protocol calls (matching chat-76's observation that Python lessons under this course's authorship tend to import typing/dataclasses for surface annotations but not actually exercise the more advanced architectural lever the brief hypothesizes). **ADVANCES GENRES module 4/9 → 5/9 partial at chat-79 M1; Lesson body region read in two passes (head-200 then head-1000 covering ~58% of the ~61.5 KB file plus tail-200 covering the chat-39 TBD scaffold and end-matter): standard chat-39 TBD scaffold confirmed in place at end-of-file with full-stem h2 id `practice-exercise-build-genres-rpg` (per the established `practice-exercise-build-{full-stem}` pattern), 3 quiz-question divs each with B-correct shape-1 attributes (`data-correct="false"`/`data-correct="true"` — to be flipped to shape-2 outer-single-quotes per chat-57-close codification at M1), literal U+2014 em-dash codepoint already present in scaffold's 'Objective: TBD — to be filled in chat 40+.' line confirming continued retrieval-discipline alignment. **Lesson IS the JS-implementation companion of the upcoming chat-79 `genres_rpg_python.html`** per the brief's pre-read hypothesis — the lesson's end-matter explicitly says 'See the complete Python implementation for the full code including Character classes, Inventory system, Quest management, Skill trees, Crafting system, and Trading mechanics' confirming the JS-then-pygame pairing pattern from chat-75 puzzle / chat-76 puzzle_python carries forward to chat-78 rpg / chat-79 rpg_python. The lesson features a full JS+HTML5-canvas RPG demo on an 800×600 canvas: (i) RPGSystem class with character/inventory/quests/skillTree/npcs/enemies/particles/floatingTexts state; (ii) Character creation switching base stats by class (warrior boosts STR/VIT/maxHp; mage boosts INT/maxMp; rogue boosts DEX/critChance/speed; cleric boosts INT/VIT/maxMp); (iii) Inventory: 40-slot `new Array(40).fill(null)`, addItem stacks consumables-by-name and otherwise allocates next empty slot; (iv) Equipment: weapon/armor/accessory slots stored as `inventory.equipment[slot]`, equipItem subtracts-prior-bonuses-then-adds-new-bonuses in lock-step pairs maintained on `character.bonusStrength`/etc.; (v) updateStats composes `attack = 15 + strength + bonusStrength + (weapon.stats.attack || 0)` per render; (vi) gainExperience uses `while (experience >= experienceToNext) { levelUp(); }` to handle multi-level XP grants; levelUp does `experienceToNext = Math.floor(experienceToNext * 1.5)` producing a stateful exponential 1.5^(level-1) curve; (vii) Quest objectives are tested INDEPENDENTLY via `every(o => o.completed)` — NOT chained; updateQuestProgress uses STRING-MATCHING on objective.text (`text.includes('level')`, `text.includes('enemies')`) to advance; (viii) NPCs have `dialogue` arrays where each node is `{text, responses: [{text, next, quest?}]}` and `next` is an integer index back into the array (or -1 = end), encoding the dialogue's branching state-machine as DATA; (ix) Skill tree dict keyed by class with each skill having optional `requirement: 'power_strike:3'` string-encoded prerequisite; (x) Combat: `damage = max(1, baseAttack - defense + random(-5..5))` then `isCrit ? damage * 2 : damage`; (xi) Save/load via `localStorage.setItem('rpgSave', JSON.stringify({character, inventory, quests}))`. **Three orthogonal axes confirmed after lesson body read, with significant divergence from the chat-78 brief's pre-read hypotheses:** (a) **Dialogue-tree-as-index-pointer-graph at NARRATIVE-FLOW scope** — each NPC's `dialogue` field is an array of `{text, responses: [{text, next, quest?}]}` nodes where `next` is an integer index back into the array (`next: 1`, `next: 2`) or `next: -1` for end-of-conversation; this encodes the dialogue's branching state-machine as DATA the renderer indexes into, NOT as scattered control flow with hardcoded if-elif chains per branch; adding a new dialogue branch is a single new array element + one `next: <new-index>` pointer edit with zero changes to the renderer's traversal loop; same data-driven externalization pattern as architecture_save_load schema chat-58 + pathfinding terrain-cost dict chat-60 + behavior-trees child-list-order chat-61 + decision-making personality dict chat-62 + procedural generation seed chat-68 + publishing_executables .spec chat-70 + publishing_marketing pitch templates chat-71 + publishing_performance algorithmic-axis chat-72 + publishing_platforms TARGETS+ADAPTERS chat-73 + publishing_updates CADENCES+MIGRATIONS chat-74 + genres_puzzle 2D-array board chat-75 + genres_puzzle_python 2D-array board chat-76 + genres_racing TRACKS dict chat-77 applied at NARRATIVE-FLOW scope = **TWENTIETH lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8, FIRST applied at NARRATIVE-FLOW scope** where the dialogue's branching graph IS data the renderer reads. **(This axis REPLACES the chat-78 brief's pre-read hypothesis (a) Stat-system-as-data-table at STAT-DEFINITION scope** — the lesson stores stats as flat properties on character (strength/intelligence/dexterity/vitality + bonusStrength/bonusIntelligence/etc.) NOT as a dict keyed by stat name; the data-driven shape lives at the dialogue layer, not the stat layer.) (b) **Equipment-bonus-as-bidirectionally-maintained-cached-state at STAT-COMPOSITION scope** — the lesson's `equipItem()` does subtract-prior-bonuses THEN add-new-bonuses in lock-step pairs maintained on `character.bonusStrength`/`bonusIntelligence`/`bonusDexterity`/`bonusVitality` as INCREMENTALLY-CACHED accumulators; per-frame `updateStats()` reads `attack = 15 + strength + bonusStrength + (weapon.stats.attack || 0)` from the cache rather than iterating over currently-equipped items each render; the cached-write makes per-frame reads O(1) at the cost of pairing unequip and equip into required-paired double-writes (forgetting the subtract-on-unequip half = bonus drifts forever and never matches reality, the classic stat-bug source); the on-demand alternative `getBonusStrength() { return Object.values(equipment).reduce((a, e) => a + (e?.stats?.strength || 0), 0); }` would make write/read order irrelevant but pay per-frame iteration cost across N equipment slots. Same pay-once-amortize-thereafter pattern category as chat-72 publishing_performance's CIRCLE_CACHE blit-vs-rasterize at COMPUTATION-COST scope and chat-64 particle_effects's max_lifetime snapshot at OBJECT-LIFECYCLE scope, here applied at STAT-COMPOSITION scope where the 'thing computed once per equip-event' is the bonus delta and the 'reuse forever (until next equip-event)' is the cached `character.bonusStrength` field read every render. **(This axis is a NEW slot replacing the chat-78 brief's pre-read hypothesis (a)'s stat-as-data-dict framing with the actual architectural lever the lesson exercises — bidirectionally-maintained cache vs on-demand recompute.)** (c) **XP-curve-as-stateful-self-multiplying-exponential at LEVEL-PROGRESSION scope** — `this.character.experienceToNext = Math.floor(this.character.experienceToNext * 1.5)` updates the NEXT-LEVEL threshold each level-up via multiplicative scaling on the CURRENT threshold value, producing a 1.5^(level-1) exponential curve as a SIDE EFFECT of repeated stateful updates rather than as a pure function `xpForLevel(level) = 100 * Math.pow(1.5, level - 1)` that supports random-access queries (e.g., 'what's xpToNext for level 17 from level 1?' without simulating 16 multiplications) or as a hardcoded lookup table `XP_TABLE = [0, 100, 250, 475, ...]` that requires touching every entry on rebalance and silently caps progression at the table length. Multi-level XP grants use `while (experience >= experienceToNext) { levelUp(); }` precisely because each levelUp call mutates BOTH `experience -= experienceToNext` AND `experienceToNext *= 1.5` — skipping a single levelUp call breaks the curve permanently because the threshold update is gated on the call. Three encoding choices (stateful self-multiply / pure function / lookup table) span a maintainability-vs-efficiency-vs-randomness-of-access tradeoff; the lesson chose stateful for locality and simplicity. **(This axis takes the chat-78 brief's pre-read hypothesis (b) slot but reframes — the lesson's actual choice is a third option (stateful self-multiply) not in the brief's binary 'function-vs-table' framing.)** Cross-references chat-58 architecture_save_load (schema-as-frozen-contract carry-forward applied to NARRATIVE-FLOW scope at axis (a) where each dialogue node IS a frozen contract for its index position and the responses' `next` pointers ARE the chain-of-frozen-contracts threading through the array), chat-72 publishing_performance (pay-once-amortize-thereafter pattern at COMPUTATION-COST scope directly extended to STAT-COMPOSITION scope at axis (b) where the equipment-bonus delta is computed once per equip-event and read every frame), and chat-77 genres_racing (checkpoint-index-as-ordered-progression-counter at RACE-PROGRESSION scope adjacent to chat-78's level-counter at LEVEL-PROGRESSION scope at axis (c) where both are integer-valued progression state mutated by event-driven hooks). **Brief's pre-read hypothesis (c) Quest-progression as ordered-state-machine DID NOT match what the lesson actually shows** — the lesson treats quest objectives as PARALLEL/UNORDERED via `quest.objectives.every(o => o.completed)` (ALL objectives must complete but in ANY order), not as a chained ordered prerequisite sequence; `updateQuestProgress` uses fragile string-matching on `objective.text.includes('level')` etc. to advance specific objectives without any declared advance-order. **ADVANCES GENRES module 3/9 → 4/9 partial at chat-78 M1; module-completeness stays 12/13** since genres doesn't close in one chat (5 genres lessons remain after chat 78: rpg_python / strategy / strategy_python / tower_defense / tower_defense_python). M0 closes ANCHOR-CLEAN; proceeding to M1 lesson HTML edit + catalog flip in object-form `quiz_topics` shape (20th consecutive cohort applying the firmly-confirmed convention).

Demo has three labeled regions visible per frame on an 800×400 canvas: LEFT panel (x: 10) renders the dialogue's current node text and its numbered responses with each response showing its `next:` integer pointer (`next=1`, `next=2`, `next=-1`); TOP-RIGHT panel (x: 420) renders 'EQUIPMENT (E equip random / U unequip):' with the equipped weapon name + strength-bonus, three lines `character.strength`, `character.bonusStrength` (cached), and TOTAL composed value in green; BOTTOM panel (x: 10, y: 220) renders 'XP CURVE (X grant 50 XP):' with level/xp/xpToNext labels, the literal stateful-rule string `xpToNext = floor(xpToNext * 1.5)` as a HUD label, and a 400×24 progress bar with a green inner fill at width `(character.xp / character.xpToNext) * 398`. Three orthogonal disciplines visible per frame as concrete renderer-read operations: dialogue's `dialogue[dlgNode]` index lookup (the dispatch IS the index), equipment's `character.bonusStrength` field read (the bonus IS cached), and xp curve's `character.xpToNext` field read (the threshold IS state). Three quiz Qs covering all three axes (B-correct in each per the canonical position): (Q1) dialogue-tree-as-index-pointer-graph at NARRATIVE-FLOW scope (each dialogue node is an array element indexed by integer and each response carries `next: <int>` (or -1) routing the conversation as data the renderer indexes into; adding a new branch is a single new array element + one pointer edit with zero changes to the renderer's traversal loop; same data-driven externalization pattern from chat-58 schema-as-frozen-contract through chat-77 TRACKS dict applied at NARRATIVE-FLOW scope = TWENTIETH lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8, FIRST applied at NARRATIVE-FLOW scope; distractor A = performance-as-driver anti-model conflating O(1) dispatch with maintainability driver; distractor C = memory-as-driver anti-model treating per-branch RAM as design driver rather than maintainability + Open/Closed Principle satisfaction); (Q2) equipment-bonus-as-bidirectionally-maintained-cached-state at STAT-COMPOSITION scope (`character.bonusStrength` is a CACHED MATERIALIZED VIEW of 'sum over currently-equipped items of their strength bonus'; without the subtract-on-unequip half the cache drifts permanently because the prior weapon's stats are never removed and bonusStrength no longer matches reality, the classic stat-bug source; the on-demand alternative `getBonusStrength()` iterating equipment makes write/read order irrelevant but pays per-frame iteration cost; the lesson chose cached-write because per-frame reads happen vastly more often than equip-events; same pay-once-amortize-thereafter pattern as chat-72 publishing_performance's CIRCLE_CACHE blit-vs-rasterize at COMPUTATION-COST scope applied at STAT-COMPOSITION scope; distractor A = fictitious-Number-precision-mechanism anti-model since equipment values are small integers and float arithmetic on integer inputs in this range is exact; distractor C = fictitious-intermediate-state-requirement anti-model since the renderer doesn't care about intermediate states between subtract and add as the operations run in synchronous JS so no intermediate is ever visible to render()); (Q3) xp-curve-as-stateful-self-multiplying-exponential at LEVEL-PROGRESSION scope (`xpToNext = Math.floor(xpToNext * 1.5)` updates the NEXT-LEVEL threshold each level-up via multiplicative scaling on the CURRENT threshold value, producing 1.5^(level-1) curve as a side effect of repeated stateful updates rather than as pure function `xpForLevel(level) = 100 * Math.pow(1.5, level - 1)` which supports random-access queries via `pow()` per query, or as hardcoded lookup table which requires touching every entry on rebalance and silently caps at table length; multi-level XP grants use `while (xp >= xpToNext) { levelUp(); }` precisely because each levelUp call mutates BOTH `xp -= xpToNext` AND `xpToNext *= 1.5` so skipping a single levelUp call breaks the curve permanently — the stateful approach is fragile to skipped level-ups since the threshold update is gated on the call, but locally efficient with all curve state in a single mutable field; three encoding choices span a maintainability-vs-efficiency-vs-randomness-of-access tradeoff and the lesson chose stateful for locality and simplicity; distractor A = performance-as-driver anti-model since stateful self-multiply happens once per level-up event which is rare so the FPS difference between approaches is unmeasurable; distractor C = fictitious-pow-precision-mechanism anti-model since Math.pow on small integer exponents and a base of 1.5 produces exact-integer-equivalent results within Number precision after the floor() call). All three quiz questions used shape-2 outer-single-quote attribute values per chat-57-close codification (`data-correct='false'`/`data-correct='true'` with `&apos;` for embedded apostrophes and `&quot;` for embedded double quotes — **25TH consecutive cohort post-codification chat-54–chat-78**); literal U+2014 em-dash codepoints throughout for the **25TH consecutive chat 54–78 M1**; HTML-escaped `&lt;` (multiple occurrences in `next: <int>` interpolations and in `next: <new-index>` references inside attribute values) and `&gt;` (multiple occurrences in `>=` comparison operators in the JS code block including `while (character.xp &gt;= character.xpToNext)`, `if ((k === '1' || k === '2') &amp;&amp; dlgNode &gt;= 0)`, `if (dlgNode &gt;= 0)`, plus `=&gt;` arrow functions in `addEventListener('keydown', e =&gt; {})` and `forEach((r, i) =&gt; {})`, plus `-&gt; next=` HUD label string) inside the Example Solution `<pre><code>` block per chat-40-onward HTML-escape discipline (**38 consecutive cohorts including chat-78**). Finding-10 EXTRA-SCRUTINY pre-check on genres_puzzle_python.html per chat-62/63 .bak-baseline date+size refinement: `.bak` = 32,658 bytes modified Wed Apr 29 2026 13:45:15 (pre-chat-39 baseline ✅; SAME Apr 29 .bak snapshot date as the publishing-module .bak files — distinct from chat-75's genres_puzzle.bak May 01 — confirming the Apr 29 snapshot IS the broader .bak pass that covered most chat-39 lessons including this one, while chat-75's genres_puzzle was apparently re-snapshotted in a later May 01 pass); `.html` = 35,279 bytes modified Tue May 05 2026 05:04:40 (chat-39 injection window ✅, matches the May 05 mod-date pattern of all chat-39-scaffolded lessons); delta = 2,621 bytes matches expected ~2.5–3 KB chat-39 TBD scaffold delta ✅; `.bak` mod-date predates `.html` mod-date ✅ — ANCHOR-CLEAN as anticipated; no Finding-14 invocation triggered (Finding 14 stays dormant on chat-76 M0 against the lesson target itself; trends toward THIRTEENTH consecutive end-to-end-clean cohort since chat 61 from a startup standpoint pending M1+M2 close). Lesson body region read in two passes (head-200 then view_range 220-500 covering the full ~35 KB file): standard chat-39 TBD scaffold confirmed in place at end-of-file with full-stem h2 id `practice-exercise-build-genres-puzzle-python` (per the established `practice-exercise-build-{full-stem}` pattern), 3 quiz-question divs each with B-correct shape-1 attributes (`data-correct="false"`/`data-correct="true"` — to be flipped to shape-2 outer-single-quotes per chat-57-close codification at M1), literal U+2014 em-dash codepoint already present in scaffold's 'Objective: TBD — to be filled in chat 40+.' line confirming continued retrieval-discipline alignment. **The lesson IS the pygame-implementation companion of chat-75's JS-implementation `genres_puzzle.html` per the brief's pre-read hypothesis** — same five sub-genres (Match-3 with cascading combos / Sliding 4×4 numbered tiles / Physics projectile-with-gravity-and-3-targets / Pattern Simon-style memory / Logic AND/OR/NOT/XOR/NAND/NOR gates) across distinct classes Match3Game / SlidingPuzzle / PhysicsPuzzle / PatternPuzzle / LogicPuzzle, plus a LogicGate helper class and a PuzzleGameManager orchestrator with screen / clock / score / time_elapsed / moves state. **Three Python-specific deltas confirmed after lesson body read, with significant divergence from the brief's pre-read hypotheses:** (1) the lesson uses `class PuzzleType(Enum): MATCH3 = "match3"; SLIDING = "sliding"; PHYSICS = "physics"; LOGIC = "logic"; PATTERN = "pattern"` for puzzle-type identifiers and the manager's `puzzles = {PuzzleType.MATCH3: Match3Game(), PuzzleType.SLIDING: SlidingPuzzle(), PuzzleType.PHYSICS: PhysicsPuzzle(...), PuzzleType.PATTERN: PatternPuzzle(), PuzzleType.LOGIC: LogicPuzzle()}` dict is keyed by the Enum value, NOT by the bare strings the chat-75 JS lesson used; (2) the lesson does NOT use `typing.Protocol` or ABC for the puzzle-genre interface — it imports `from typing import List, Tuple, Optional, Dict` for method-signature annotations only (e.g., `def swap_gems(self, x1: int, y1: int, x2: int, y2: int) -> bool:`) and the five puzzle classes remain duck-typed without any explicit shared interface declaration; the manager's `handle_click` and `render_*` methods even retain explicit `if self.current_puzzle == PuzzleType.MATCH3: ... elif PuzzleType.SLIDING: ...` branches per puzzle type rather than the JS lesson's `PUZZLES[active].handle_click(...)` polymorphic single-call shape; (3) the lesson does NOT use `@dataclass` for board state (imports it but never decorates a class) and does NOT use `itertools.product` or `collections.deque` for grid algorithms — the grid traversals are nested for-loops `for y in range(grid_size): for x in range(grid_size):` and the cascade is RECURSIVE (process_matches calls itself when new_matches is non-empty: `new_matches = self.find_matches(); if new_matches: self.combo += 1; self.process_matches(new_matches)`) rather than the chat-75 JS lesson's iterative `combo = 0; while self.step(): combo += 1`. **Brief's pre-read hypotheses (a) Protocol-formality, (b) @dataclass-frozen, (c) itertools/deque ALL did not match what the lesson actually shows; revised three orthogonal axes after lesson body read:** (a) **Enum-based puzzle-type identity at PUZZLE-IDENTITY scope** — `class PuzzleType(Enum)` enumerates the five valid puzzle identities at design-time so a typo `PuzzleType.MATC3` raises AttributeError at the import statement of the typo-containing module rather than `puzzles['matc3']` silently returning None at dispatch time; mypy can also verify `current_puzzle: PuzzleType` annotations at design time and reject any string literal that doesn't match a declared Enum member; same design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery pattern as chat-47 platformer_level_design's validate-vs-is_solid + chat-70 publishing_executables's hiddenimports static-AST-vs-runtime-discovery + chat-72 publishing_performance's profile-bars-vs-intuition + chat-73 publishing_platforms's try-import runtime-capability-detection applied at PUZZLE-IDENTITY scope = **FIFTH lesson reinforcing the design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery pattern across Phase 8, FIRST applied at PUZZLE-IDENTITY scope** where the design-time hypothesis is 'this puzzle name exists' and the runtime discovery is the dispatch lookup either succeeding or raising. **This axis REPLACES the brief's pre-read hypothesis (a) Protocol-formality** — Protocol is a different design-time validation tool operating at the INTERFACE scope (what methods must exist) while Enum operates at the IDENTITY scope (which names exist and how they're spelled); the lesson's Python-specific addition over chat-75's JS implementation is the Enum, not a Protocol. (b) **2D-array board state reaffirmed at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope** — Match3Game's `self.grid = [[gem_type ...] for ...]` (8×8 ints 0–5 plus -1 for cleared cells) and SlidingPuzzle's `self.grid` (4×4 ints 0–15 with 0 = empty slot) both share the nested-list-of-ints shape that the chat-75 JS lesson also used; same data-driven externalization pattern as architecture_save_load schema chat-58 + pathfinding terrain-cost dict chat-60 + behavior-trees child-list-order chat-61 + decision-making personality dict chat-62 + procedural generation seed chat-68 + publishing_executables .spec file chat-70 + publishing_marketing pitch templates chat-71 + publishing_performance algorithmic-axis toggles chat-72 + publishing_platforms TARGETS+ADAPTERS dicts chat-73 + publishing_updates CADENCES+MIGRATIONS dicts chat-74 + genres_puzzle 2D-array board chat-75 applied at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope = **EIGHTEENTH lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8, REAFFIRMING chat-75's FIRST BOARD-REPRESENTATION application in Python where the @dataclass import is unused and the board IS a raw nested list of ints**. **This axis MATCHES the brief's pre-read hypothesis (b) BOARD-STRUCTURE but with the realization that the lesson's `from dataclasses import dataclass` import is unused** — the board is raw `[[int]]` not `@dataclass(frozen=True)`-wrapped; the data-driven externalization shape is identical to chat-75's JS, just expressed in Python's list-of-list syntax instead of JS's array-of-array. (c) **Recursive cascade fixed-point at MATCH-CASCADE scope** — Match3Game's `process_matches(matches)` recursively calls itself with `new_matches = self.find_matches(); if new_matches: self.combo += 1; self.process_matches(new_matches)`; this is the same fixed-point shape as chat-75's JS `combo = 0; while self.step(): combo += 1` but expressed as Python-natural recursion rather than iteration; the recursion terminates because the int-valued grid has finitely many states and clearing strictly reduces the count of non-cleared cells, so the recursion must reach a base case (find_matches returns empty → no recursive call); same chained-contract pattern as chat-74 publishing_updates' MIGRATIONS chain where each migration step is a frozen contract that may produce a new state requiring another step, here applied at MATCH-CASCADE scope where each recursive call is a frozen contract that may produce new matches requiring another call. **This axis MATCHES the brief's pre-read hypothesis (c) but expresses the cascade via Python recursion not via itertools/deque** — the lesson's nested for-loops in find_matches and drop_gems are NOT modernized to itertools.product, but the recursion-vs-iteration distinction is the cleaner Python-specific delta from chat-75 since both forms are valid Python and the recursive choice IS the architecturally expressive shape for a fixed-point computation that natively threads the combo counter through the call stack rather than requiring an outer accumulator. **ADVANCES GENRES module 1/9 → 2/9 partial at chat-76 M1; module-completeness stays 12/13** since genres doesn't close in one chat (7 genres lessons remain after chat 76: racing / rpg / rpg_python / strategy / strategy_python / tower_defense / tower_defense_python). M0 closes ANCHOR-CLEAN; proceeding to M1 lesson HTML edit + catalog flip in object-form `quiz_topics` shape (18th consecutive cohort applying the firmly-confirmed convention).

Lesson covers FIVE distinct puzzle sub-genres in a single interactive demo: Match-3 (8×8 gem grid with 6 colors, click-to-select-then-swap with one-step adjacency check, no cascade in JS demo despite description mentioning combos), Sliding-puzzles (4×4 with 1–15 + 0-empty, 100-iteration random-walk shuffle with valid-move constraint, `checkWin()` linear scan), Physics-puzzles (projectile with gravity, click-to-aim launch, 3 randomly-placed targets with circle-distance hit detection), Pattern-memory (Simon-style 4-button color sequence with progressive-length growth on success and reset on miss), and Logic-gates (3 boolean inputs A/B/C, AND-gate output, click-to-toggle). The unifying architecture is an explicit polymorphic-dispatch pattern: `PuzzleGame.puzzles = {match3: new Match3Puzzle, sliding: new SlidingPuzzle, physics: new PhysicsPuzzle, pattern: new PatternPuzzle, logic: new LogicPuzzle}` dict + uniform `init()/handleClick(mx,my)/update()/render()/hint()/shuffle()` interface across all five classes; the controller's `handleClick(e)`, `gameLoop()`, `reset()`, `hint()`, `shuffle()` methods all dispatch via `this.puzzles[this.currentPuzzle].method(...)` without ever branching on `currentPuzzle` value — the dict-index IS the polymorphic dispatch. Lesson then covers Best Practices (Clear Rules / Progressive Difficulty / Visual Feedback / No Dead Ends / Hint Systems / Satisfying Effects / Multiple Solutions / Undo Feature) and Key Takeaways (8 emoji-bulleted items including procedural-generation-for-replayability). **M1 pick — three orthogonal axes confirmed after lesson body read, with delta noted from chat-75 brief pre-read hypotheses:** (a) **Polymorphic puzzle-genre dispatch at PUZZLE-GENRE scope** — the lesson's central architectural pattern with `puzzles = {match3, sliding, physics, pattern, logic}` dict + uniform `init()/handleClick()/update()/render()` interface; adding a sixth genre (e.g., word puzzles per the lesson's mentioned-but-not-implemented sixth) = one new class + one dict entry, zero changes to controller dispatch code; Open/Closed Principle satisfied at PUZZLE-GENRE scope; same UIManager-polymorphic-dispatch pattern from chat-67 graphics_ui_hud + same PlatformAdapter pattern from chat-73 publishing_platforms applied at PUZZLE-GENRE scope = SECOND lesson reinforcing the polymorphic-dispatch-via-shared-protocol pattern at a new domain scope (after chat-73's PLATFORM-API scope), FIRST applied at PUZZLE-GENRE scope. **(This axis REPLACES the chat-75 brief's pre-read hypothesis (a) BOARD-REPRESENTATION-vs-OOP-cells which was too narrow — the lesson's lead architectural idea is the 5-genre uniform interface, not the inside-match-3 grid-vs-cell debate.)** (b) **Grid-state-as-2D-array at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope** — match-3 uses `grid[y][x] = color_int` (8×8, ints 0–5) and sliding uses `grid[y][x] = number` (4×4, ints 0–15 with 0 = empty); the 2D-array shape is shared between the two grid-based puzzle genres and is dramatically simpler to clone (for undo), serialize (for save), pass to detection algorithms (match-finding) and compare (for win-check) than a parallel `Cell` object graph would be; same data-driven externalization pattern as architecture_save_load schema chat-58 + pathfinding terrain-cost dict chat-60 + behavior-trees child-list-order chat-61 + decision-making personality dict chat-62 + procedural generation seed chat-68 + publishing_executables .spec file chat-70 + publishing_marketing pitch templates chat-71 + publishing_performance algorithmic-axis toggles chat-72 + publishing_platforms TARGETS+ADAPTERS dicts chat-73 + publishing_updates CADENCES dict chat-74 applied at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope = SEVENTEENTH lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8, FIRST applied at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope where the board IS the data the puzzle's algorithms (swap, slide, match-detect, cascade) read and mutate. **(This axis TAKES the chat-75 brief's pre-read hypothesis (a) at the new (b) slot.)** (c) **Match-cascade-as-fixed-point-loop at MATCH-CASCADE scope** — match-3's full mechanic (mentioned in lesson description but not implemented in JS demo) is `while step(): combo += 1` where each `step()` does {detect matches → clear matched cells → apply gravity dropping remaining tiles → spawn new tiles from top → return True if any change happened, False if state stabilized}; same fixed-point-iteration shape as chat-74 publishing_updates' MIGRATIONS chain (each iteration is a frozen contract that may produce a new state requiring another iteration) applied at MATCH-CASCADE scope, with combo multiplier as natural by-product of iteration count; folds the brief's pre-read hypothesis (b) MATCH-DETECTION (flood-fill vs nested-loop) INTO this axis as one component of the per-iteration step rather than promoting it to its own axis (BOARD-REP at (b) and MATCH-CASCADE at (c) are more orthogonal as a pair than MATCH-DETECTION vs CASCADE would be — the latter pair both live inside the cascade step). **(This axis MATCHES the chat-75 brief's pre-read hypothesis (c).)** Cross-references chat-58 architecture_save_load (schema-as-frozen-contract carry-forward applied to BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope at axis (b): a 2D `board[row][col] = color_int` array IS a frozen data contract that match-detection / cascade / serialization all read from), chat-67 graphics_ui_hud (UIElement-protocol-vs-isinstance-branches pattern directly extended to PUZZLE-GENRE scope at axis (a) where each puzzle class implements a uniform interface and the controller dispatches polymorphically), chat-73 publishing_platforms (PlatformAdapter pattern at PLATFORM-API scope adjacent to chat-75's PuzzleGenre pattern at PUZZLE-GENRE scope — both establish polymorphic dispatch at different domain scopes), and chat-74 publishing_updates (MIGRATIONS chained-contract pattern at SAVE-MIGRATION scope directly extended to MATCH-CASCADE scope at axis (c) where each cascade iteration is a frozen contract that may produce a new state requiring another iteration). **OPENS GENRES module 0/9 → 1/9 partial at chat-75 M1; module-completeness stays 12/13** since genres doesn't close in one chat (8 genres lessons remain after chat 75: puzzle_python / racing / rpg / rpg_python / strategy / strategy_python / tower_defense / tower_defense_python).
