Three orthogonal disciplines visible per frame as concrete dict entries (the 5 PUZZLES rows on the LEFT, dispatch routing through `PUZZLES[active].method(...)` with zero per-genre branching anywhere in the controller's event loop), board values (the MIDDLE-panel grid renders read directly from `match3.grid[r][c]` and `sliding.grid[r][c]` ints — same 2D-array shape across both grid-based genres), and iteration counts (the RIGHT-panel combo counter IS the cascade loop's iteration count without any extra accumulator — `combo = 0; while self.step(): combo += 1` where step() returns True iff the grid changed). Three quiz Qs covering all three axes (B-correct in each per the canonical position): (Q1) polymorphic puzzle-genre dispatch via shared protocol at PUZZLE-GENRE scope (every genre class implements the same handle_click / render / step interface and the controller calls `PUZZLES[active].method(...)` once with no per-genre branching anywhere, so adding a sixth genre word_puzzles = one new class plus one new dict entry with zero edits to the controller's event loop or render orchestrator; same UIElement-protocol pattern from chat-67 graphics_ui_hud and PlatformAdapter pattern from chat-73 publishing_platforms applied at PUZZLE-GENRE scope = SECOND polymorphic-dispatch lesson reinforcing the shared-protocol pattern at a new domain scope; distractor A = dict-lookup-performance anti-model conflating O(1) dispatch cost with the actual architectural driver of controller-code modularity; distractor C = memory-as-driver anti-model treating dict-stored-instance-overhead as the design driver rather than controller-code modularity); (Q2) grid-state-as-2D-array at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope (match-3 stores its 8×8 board as `grid[r][c] = color_int` with values 0–5 plus −1 for cleared cells and sliding stores its 4×4 board as `grid[r][c] = number` with values 0–15 (0 = empty) — both genres share the same 2D-array shape so swap and slide are both two-line index-pair assignments, win-check is a flat scan, match-detect is two nested for-loops over (r, c), serialization is one `json.dumps` call, and undo is one list-comprehension deep-copy; same data-driven externalization pattern as architecture_save_load schema chat-58 + pathfinding terrain-cost dict chat-60 + behavior-trees child-list-order chat-61 + decision-making personality dict chat-62 + procedural generation seed chat-68 + publishing_executables .spec file chat-70 + publishing_marketing pitch templates chat-71 + publishing_performance algorithmic-axis toggles chat-72 + publishing_platforms TARGETS dict chat-73 + publishing_updates CADENCES + MIGRATIONS dicts chat-74 applied at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope = **SEVENTEENTH lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8, FIRST applied at BOARD-REPRESENTATION scope** where the board IS the data the puzzle's algorithms (swap, slide, match-detect, cascade) read and mutate; distractor A = parallel-Cell-object-graph anti-model claiming row/col/color attributes plus four neighbor pointers is conceptually cleaner — actually every swap/slide becomes 'rebind two object refs plus update each Cell's row/col fields plus traverse neighbor pointers', save/load needs custom __init__ logic per Cell type, match-detect needs object-identity comparison rather than int equality; distractor C = static-type-safety anti-model claiming plain int values give mypy more information than Cell instances — actually Python is duck-typed and both shapes can be annotated equivalently; the architectural reason is operation-site simplicity, not static type checks); (Q3) match-cascade-as-fixed-point-loop at MATCH-CASCADE scope (match-3's handle_click ends with `combo = 0; while self.step(): combo += 1` where step() is a frozen contract that takes the current grid and produces either a strictly different grid (returns True) or the same grid (returns False); the loop converges because the int-valued grid has finitely many states and clearing strictly reduces the count of marked cells, so the iteration must reach a stable state; the combo multiplier IS the iteration count without any extra accumulator — every True return increments combo by exactly one; same chained-contract pattern as chat-74 publishing_updates' MIGRATIONS dict (each iteration is a frozen contract that may produce a new state requiring another iteration) applied at MATCH-CASCADE scope; distractor A = bounded-MAX_CASCADE_DEPTH anti-model claiming a `for _ in range(MAX_CASCADE_DEPTH): self.step()` loop avoids unbounded-while risk — actually the fixed-point loop terminates exactly when no further matches exist regardless of depth, while a bounded loop caps combo artificially even when more matches exist after the limit AND runs unnecessary iterations on simple swaps where step() returned False after one pass; distractor C = combo-threaded-into-step anti-model claiming the combo counter must be threaded into step() itself — actually the iteration count of the outer while loop already IS the combo, and threading state into step() couples the cascade primitive to its caller's bookkeeping; the clean shape keeps step() focused on grid transitions and lets the outer loop count its own iterations). Steam-the-Giant `SteamIntegration` class wrapping the steamworks library via `try: import steamworks except ImportError: steamworks = None` with methods `initialize()` / `get_user_info()` / `unlock_achievement(achievement_name)` / `set_rich_presence(key, value)` / `get_leaderboard(leaderboard_name, num_entries)` / `submit_score(leaderboard_name, score)` / `shutdown()` — every method guarded with `if not self.initialized: return False` so the game runs unmodified whether Steam is available or not (STEAM_APP_ID = 480 Spacewar test app); itch.io-Indie-Paradise Butler CLI (`butler push mygame-windows.zip username/game-name:windows --userversion 1.0.0`) + `ItchIOAPI` class with `get_my_games()` / `get_game_stats(game_id)` / `post_devlog(game_id, title, body, status)`; Mobile Distribution `MobileBuildConfig` with self.config = {"android": {package_name, version_code, min_sdk, target_sdk, permissions, signing}, "ios": {bundle_id, version, build, min_ios, device_capabilities, orientations, info_plist}} dict-of-platform-configs + `generate_android_manifest()` / `generate_info_plist()` methods + `AppStoreConnect` class with JWT-token-based upload pipeline; Web Distribution hosting-options list + Web Monetization API + AdSense + Stripe IAP code; Platform Comparison table (Best For / Discovery / Competition / Features / Marketing across Steam/itch/Epic/Mobile); Multi-Platform Strategy release-timeline Mermaid Gantt (Pre-Launch → Launch → Post-Launch with itch.io Alpha → Steam Early Access → Full Steam/Epic Release → Mobile Ports → Console Ports recommended order); Platform-Specific Features Steam list (Achievements / Trading Cards / Cloud Saves / Workshop / Leaderboards / Rich Presence / Remote Play / Steam Deck verified) + Mobile list (Push Notifications / IAP / Ad Monetization / Game Center / Cloud Save / Social Sharing / Analytics / Crash Reporting); Best Practices Start Early / Cross-Promote / Platform Features / Regional Pricing / Localization / Reviews / Updates / Analytics / Community / Compliance. **M1 pick — three orthogonal axes confirmed after lesson body read:** (a) **Platform-abstraction-layer as polymorphic-dispatch via shared protocol at PLATFORM-API scope** — SteamIntegration / ItchIOAPI / AppStoreConnect each wrap a different backend library (Steamworks / itch REST API / App Store Connect JWT) but every game needs the SAME conceptual operations regardless of which platform is currently active: unlock an achievement, submit a score, set a presence string, post a devlog, get a leaderboard. The Open/Closed Principle says if the game has `if platform == 'steam': steam.unlock_achievement(...) elif platform == 'itch': itch.post_devlog(...)` branches scattered through update() and score() and quest-completion paths, adding a new platform requires N edits across the codebase. With a shared `PlatformAdapter` protocol providing a uniform interface (e.g., `unlock_achievement(name)`, `submit_score(score)`, `set_presence(key, val)`, `post_devlog(title, body)`) and per-platform SteamAdapter / ItchAdapter / MobileAdapter / WebAdapter implementations dispatching to their respective backend libraries, the game calls `current_platform.unlock_achievement('FIRST_LAUNCH')` once and the polymorphic dispatch routes to the right backend; adding a new platform = one new adapter class + zero edits to caller code. Same UIManager-polymorphic-dispatch pattern from chat-67 graphics_ui_hud (UIElement protocol with HealthBar / Minimap / DialogBox implementations dispatching update/render polymorphically; no isinstance branches in UIManager) applied at PLATFORM-API scope where each adapter provides the same interface backed by different platform-native implementations. (b) **Platform-capability-detection at runtime via try-import / sys.platform / hasattr at PLATFORM-CAPABILITY scope** — the lesson's `try: import steamworks except ImportError: print("Steamworks API not available"); steamworks = None` followed by `if not steamworks: return False` in `initialize()` IS the runtime-discovery instrument for platform capabilities. You CANNOT statically know at build-time whether the user's machine has steamworks installed (some Steam users have it bundled with the Steam client, some don't; some platforms aren't Steam at all); the `try: import / except ImportError` IS the runtime probe and `if not steamworks` IS the conditional that flows from it, with the lookup folding the conditional logic into the language's normal import machinery rather than scattering platform-check branches across every method that calls into Steam. Same shape as `getattr(sys, '_MEIPASS', os.path.dirname(__file__))` from chat-70 publishing_executables where the runtime lookup IS the conditional. Same design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery pattern as chat-47 platformer_level_design's validate() vs is_solid() (validate at design-time catches structural errors before shipping; is_solid at runtime catches the gameplay edge cases) and chat-70 publishing_executables's hidden_imports static-AST-vs-runtime-discovery (static AST parsing misses dynamic imports; the hiddenimports list is the explicit declaration that bridges what static analysis missed) and chat-72 publishing_performance's profile-bars vs intuition (profiler output IS the runtime discovery instrument that replaces design-time intuition about hot paths) applied at PLATFORM-CAPABILITY scope where the design-time hypothesis is 'this feature is available on this platform' and the runtime discovery is the actual import / API call succeeding or raising = FOURTH lesson reinforcing the design-time-validation-vs-runtime-discovery pattern across Phase 8, FIRST applied at PLATFORM-CAPABILITY scope. (c) **Build-target-as-data-externalization at BUILD-TARGET scope** — the lesson's `MobileBuildConfig.config = {"android": {package_name, version_code, min_sdk, target_sdk, permissions, signing}, "ios": {bundle_id, version, build, min_ios, device_capabilities, orientations, info_plist}}` dict-of-platform-configs IS the build target list externalized as data; the Platform Overview comparison table (Steam 70/30 $100 + itch.io PWYW Free + Epic 88/12 Curated + GOG 70/30 Curated + Google Play 70/30→85/15 $25 + Apple 70/30→85/15 $99/year) IS the same shape rendered as documentation. Adding a new mobile platform = one new dict entry under self.config (e.g., 'amazon_fire': {...}) rather than scattered if-elif edits across generate_*_manifest methods; adding a new desktop storefront = one new TARGETS dict entry rather than editing every fee-calculation site. Same data-driven externalization pattern as architecture_save_load schema (chat-58 at SAVE-FORMAT scope), pathfinding terrain-cost dict (chat-60 at PATHFINDING-COST scope), behavior-trees child-list-order (chat-61 at PRIORITY scope), decision-making personality dict (chat-62 at AGENT-BEHAVIOR scope), procedural generation seed (chat-68 at WORLD-IDENTITY scope), publishing_executables .spec file (chat-70 at BUILD-CONFIG scope), and publishing_marketing pitch templates + hashtag day-of-week dict + email tier templates (chat-71 at MARKETING-COPY scope), applied at BUILD-TARGET scope where the platform list IS data the build pipeline iterates over = FIFTEENTH lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8, FIRST applied at BUILD-TARGET scope where adding a new platform target is a single dict-entry edit rather than scattered control-flow changes; cross-references chat-70 publishing_executables (.spec file IS data the build pipeline reads at BUILD-CONFIG scope; chat-73's TARGETS dict IS data the build pipeline iterates over at BUILD-TARGET scope; chat-70 declares HOW to build, chat-73 declares WHERE to build to) and chat-71 publishing_marketing (per-platform marketing funnel — each platform's discovery → install → first-launch → retention pipeline is its own 5-stage funnel; same multi-stage-signal shape applied at PER-PLATFORM-FUNNEL scope as a natural extension of chat-71's MARKETING-METRICS scope). M0 closes ANCHOR-CLEAN; proceeding to M1 lesson HTML edit + catalog flip in object-form `quiz_topics` shape (15th consecutive cohort applying the firmly-confirmed convention).

(c) **Marketing-pipeline vs build-pipeline temporal-decoupling at PUBLISHING-PIPELINE scope** — marketing tracks run on calendar cadences spanning 15–180 days (Social 180d, Devlog 165d, Press Kit 90d, Trailer 30d, Influencer Outreach 45d, Launch Campaign 15d) while the build pipeline (chat-70 publishing_executables) runs on-demand whenever the developer presses build; the two pipelines share the launch date as their convergence anchor but neither blocks the other (a delayed build doesn't pause marketing; a paused marketing track doesn't break the build); same independent-pipelines-compose-via-shared-anchor pattern as chat-66 ping-pong-effects-dict / chat-67 UIElement-protocol / chat-68 height-vs-moisture-independence applied at PUBLISHING-PIPELINE scope; FIRST publishing-domain lesson establishing the marketing-pipeline-vs-build-pipeline pair-relationship at adjacent publishing-domain stages (chat-70 build = compiles source code; chat-71 marketing = produces press materials; both feed into the same launch). ## Chat 68 — ✅ closed at M2 end-to-end clean — Phase 8 question-content fill (cohort-24: graphics_procedural — 1 lesson; 14th 1-lesson cohort under chat-54-close 1-lesson cohort discipline; ADVANCED GRAPHICS module 3/5 → 4/5 partial at chat-68 M1; module-completeness stays 10/13; FIFTH chat under chat-64-startup archive-and-collapse M2-close discipline writing `support/archive/chat-68.md` as the fifth per-chat archive file; SIXTH consecutive end-to-end-clean cohort since chat 61 [chat 61 first; chat 64 second; chat 65 third (had in-chat Finding-14 resume but completed clean STARTUP); chat 66 fourth; chat 67 fifth; chat 68 sixth])

**Chat 68 closed end-to-end clean — no Finding-14 invocation needed.** M1 landed: graphics_procedural.html `done` with 'One Seed, Two Layers, Six Biomes — Seeded Multi-Octave Perlin + Independent Moisture Layer + Threshold-Rule Biome Composition in One Pygame Window' (~95-line pygame demo on a 1088×480 window with a 272×107 internal map at 4× SCALE: `fbm(x, y, octaves, ox, oy)` accumulator with `amp *= PERSISTENCE` and `freq *= LACUNARITY` per iteration; `generate(seed, octaves)` calling `random.seed(seed)` then drawing TWO independent `random.uniform(-1000, 1000)` offset pairs `(hx, hy)` and `(mx, my)` so the height map and moisture map sample completely different regions of pnoise2 space; `biome(h, m)` threshold cascade returning ocean/beach/snow/mountain/desert/grassland/forest; `render_biomes()` filling SCALE×SCALE rects per biome label; main loop with R = re-roll seed via `random.randint(0, 99999)` and 1–6 = octave count) + 3 quiz Qs covering seed-as-world-identity-at-procedural-generation-scope (the seed IS the world's identity; 8 bytes regenerates the entire 272×107 map deterministically — same compact-persistence pattern Minecraft uses to save 100+ MB of world data as an 8-byte seed; same seed-as-contract shape as chat-58 architecture_save_load's schema-as-contract; generalizes chat-43 game_mathematics_random's 'Always Use Seeds' Best Practice from per-game-event randomness to whole-world generation = EIGHTEENTH lesson reinforcing data-driven externalization across Phase 8) + multi-octave-fBm-composition-vs-single-octave-noise (`total += pnoise2(...) * amp` with geometric amplitude decay 1.0/0.5/0.25/0.125/... and geometric frequency growth 1.0/2.0/4.0/8.0/...; ## Out-of-scope flags from chat 15 (decide separately if any are worth a focused chat)

1. **`details.toc-card` floating outline overlays canvas-fallback area on mobile.** Sticky `<details class="card toc-card auto-toc">`, z-index 100, ~229 px tall, default-open. Visually covers canvas-fallback figure on phones. Pre-existing (Phase 5 auto-TOC infra). Possible fixes: default-collapsed below 768 px, fully hidden below 768 px, or shrink the sticky height.
2. **Canvas demo JS animation loops keep running on mobile when canvas is hidden** — wasted CPU. Pre-existing across all 53 canvas demos. Easy per-lesson fix (`if (matchMedia('(max-width: 768px)').matches) return;` early-out at top of animation loop) but rolling out to 53 canvases is a script-pass.
3. **Lazy-load on canvas-fallback `<img>`** is correct behavior — noted only because it caused initial diagnostic confusion (`naturalWidth: 0` on first JS query, resolves on scroll). Implication for future render checks: query `naturalWidth` AFTER scrolling into viewport.
